     <p><b>University of Waterloo</b> (commonly referred as <b>Waterloo</b> or <b>UW</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public</a> research <a href="/wiki/University" title="University">university</a> whose main campus is located in <a href="/wiki/Waterloo,_Ontario" title="Waterloo, Ontario">Waterloo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>. The main campus is located on 404 hectares (1,000 acres) of land in Uptown Waterloo, adjacent to Waterloo Park. The university offers a wide variety of academic programs, which is administered by six faculties and ten faculty-based schools. The university also operates four <a href="/wiki/Satellite_campus" title="Satellite campus">satellite campuses</a> and four <a href="/wiki/Affiliated_school" title="Affiliated school">affiliated</a> <a href="/wiki/University_colleges" title="University colleges" class="mw-redirect">university colleges</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-About_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> Waterloo is a member of the <a href="/wiki/U15_(universities)" title="U15 (universities)" class="mw-redirect">U15</a>, a group of research-intensive universities in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university traces its origins to 1 July 1957 as the Waterloo College Associate Faculties, a semi-autonomous entity of Waterloo College (which later evolved into the present-day <a href="/wiki/Wilfrid_Laurier_University" title="Wilfrid Laurier University">Wilfrid Laurier University</a>). The entity had formally separated from Waterloo College in 1959, and was incorporated as a university.<sup id="cite_ref-hist_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hist-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> The university was established in order to fill the need of a program to train engineers and technicians for Canada?s growing postwar economy. Since then, the university had greatly expanded, adding a faculty of arts in 1960, and the College of Optometry of Ontario moving from <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a> in 1967.<sup id="cite_ref-hist_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hist-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university is co-educational, and has nearly 26,000 undergraduate and over 4,000 post-graduate students. Alumni and former students of the university can be found all across Canada and in 141 countries around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-About_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> The university ranked 151-200th in the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_ARWU_CAN_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_ARWU_CAN-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> 191st in the 2012 <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-qsqs_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qsqs-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> and 226-250th in the 2012-2013 <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_THES_W_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_THES_W-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> Waterloo's varsity teams, known as the <a href="/wiki/Waterloo_Warriors" title="Waterloo Warriors">Waterloo Warriors</a> compete in the <a href="/wiki/Ontario_University_Athletics" title="Ontario University Athletics">Ontario University Athletics</a> conference of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Interuniversity_Sport" title="Canadian Interuniversity Sport">Canadian Interuniversity Sport</a>.</p>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Waterloo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width: 20%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;"> 
      <div style="position: relative; text-align: left;"> 
       <div> 
        <p>&quot;The greatest product which we will realize from our electronic era is the better educated race. This applies to all fields ? not just the field of science.&quot;</p> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <div style="text-align: left;">
       ? 
       <a href="/wiki/Ira_Needles" title="Ira Needles">Ira Needles</a>, 1956
       <sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UWaterloo_-_Douglas_Wright_Engineering_Building.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/UWaterloo_-_Douglas_Wright_Engineering_Building.JPG/200px-UWaterloo_-_Douglas_Wright_Engineering_Building.JPG" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/UWaterloo_-_Douglas_Wright_Engineering_Building.JPG/300px-UWaterloo_-_Douglas_Wright_Engineering_Building.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/UWaterloo_-_Douglas_Wright_Engineering_Building.JPG/400px-UWaterloo_-_Douglas_Wright_Engineering_Building.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UWaterloo_-_Douglas_Wright_Engineering_Building.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Constructed in 1958, the Douglas Wright Engineering Building is the oldest building that was erected for use by the university.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Waterloo was originally created in 1956 as a non-denominational board established by Waterloo College (present-day <a href="/wiki/Wilfred_Laurier_University" title="Wilfred Laurier University" class="mw-redirect">Wilfred Laurier University</a>) to obtain government grants to run expanded science programs under the name Waterloo College Associated Faculties. This non-denominational board first conducted operations in 1957 and continued to do so until 1959, when the <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Assembly_of_Ontario" title="Legislative Assembly of Ontario">Legislative Assembly of Ontario</a> passed an Act which formally split the board from Waterloo College, and reestablished it as the University of Waterloo.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>This university was established in response to community demand for improved education facilities, particularly in technical and scientific fields of study. Renowned for the success of its cooperative education programs, it now has the largest engineering school in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> The first 74 students began classes on 1 July 1957, in makeshift temporary buildings on the Waterloo College campus. In 1958, the University of Waterloo established an extension department.</p> 
     <p>In January 1958, Hagey and colleagues purchased 74 hectares (180&nbsp;acres) of farmland a kilometre west of Waterloo College's main campus in order to meet the growing expansion needs.<sup id="cite_ref-iw-uwhistory_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iw-uwhistory-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> Soon, construction began of the first academic building on the new site, known as the Chemistry and Chemical Engineering Building, later renamed Engineering 1 and now named after <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Tyndall_Wright" title="Douglas Tyndall Wright">Douglas Wright</a>, UW's first Dean of Engineering.<sup id="cite_ref-ironwarrior-eng-expansion_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ironwarrior-eng-expansion-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> Through a series of delicate negotiations which turned into bitter hostilities, the &quot;Faculty of Science and Engineering&quot; broke free from Waterloo College, partly due to the fact that the two campuses were now disjoint. Hagey himself was opposed to the break, as his dream had been to establish a world-class university built on the strengths of Waterloo College's liberal arts strengths and the applied science education of WCAF.</p> 
     <p>The University of Waterloo in <a href="/wiki/Waterloo,_Ontario" title="Waterloo, Ontario">Waterloo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a> was incorporated and granted a university charter in 1959.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> In early 1959, the government established three universities: Waterloo Lutheran University, <a href="/wiki/St._Jerome%27s_University" title="St. Jerome's University">University of St. Jerome's College</a>, and the University of Waterloo.</p> 
     <p>The policy of university education initiated in the 1960s responded to population pressure and the belief that higher education was a key to social justice and economic productivity for individuals and for society.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> The governance was modelled on the provincial University of Toronto Act of 1906 which established a bicameral system of university government consisting of a senate (faculty), responsible for academic policy, and a board of governors (citizens) exercising exclusive control over financial policy and having formal authority in all other matters. The president, appointed by the board, was to provide a link between the 2 bodies and to perform institutional leadership.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Initially, St. Jerome's and Waterloo Lutheran were both expected to federate with the new UW, but in the end Waterloo Lutheran chose to remain independent. <a href="/wiki/Waterloo_Lutheran_Seminary" title="Waterloo Lutheran Seminary">Waterloo Lutheran Seminary</a> is currently an affiliate of the nondenominational Wilfrid Laurier University and offers several programs at the master's level and a Doctor of Ministry in pastoral counselling and marriage and family therapy. The Waterloo Lutheran seminary established the Institute for Christian Ethics in 1986.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> UW then quickly created a <a href="/wiki/Liberal_arts" title="Liberal arts" class="mw-redirect">faculty of arts</a> in order to gain respect as a university. In the same year, arts students joined the science and engineering students in the new campus.</p> 
     <p>Waterloo created the first Faculty of <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">Mathematics</a> in North America, and the first co-op programs outside of engineering soon followed. The co-op system then was revised in involving four-month terms rather than the initial three-month terms. In 1967, the College of <a href="/wiki/Optometry" title="Optometry">Optometry</a> of Ontario, at the time an independent institution in Toronto, moved to Waterloo and became affiliated with the university as the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Waterloo_School_of_Optometry" title="University of Waterloo School of Optometry" class="mw-redirect">School of Optometry and Vision Science</a>. In 1967 the world's first Department of Kinesiology was created, which later grew into the Faculty of Applied <a href="/wiki/Health_science" title="Health science" class="mw-redirect">Health Sciences</a>. The Faculty of <a href="/wiki/Environmental_studies" title="Environmental studies">Environmental Studies</a> was created soon after. It was renamed the Faculty of Environment in 2008. The University of Waterloo launched its program in architecture in 1967.</p> 
     <p>In 2001, the university announced its intentions to develop a <a href="/wiki/Research_park" title="Research park">research</a> and <a href="/wiki/Science_park" title="Science park">technology park</a> in the university's north campus. The park was planned to house many of the high-tech industries in the area, supported by a comprehensive partnership between the university, the <a href="/wiki/Regional_Municipality_of_Waterloo" title="Regional Municipality of Waterloo">Regional Municipality of Waterloo</a>, the provincial and federal governments, and the <a href="/wiki/Canada%27s_Technology_Triangle" title="Canada's Technology Triangle">Canada's Technology Triangle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> The park was intended to provide businesses with access to the university's faculty, co-operative education students, alumni, as well as the university's infrastructure and resources.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sybase" title="Sybase">Sybase</a> would be the first anchor tenant of the park, with the park's groundbreaking occurring on 25 June 2002. The first building to have been completed at the park is the Sybase campus building, opening on 26 November 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2010, the Waterloo Research and Tech Park was renamed to the David Johnston Research and Technology Park. The park was named after <a href="/wiki/David_Johnston" title="David Johnston">David Johnston</a>, the 28th <a href="/wiki/Governor_General_of_Canada" title="Governor General of Canada">Governor General of Canada</a>, and former president of the university.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>From 2009 to 2012, the university had also previously managed four undergraduate programs in <a href="/wiki/Dubai_International_Academic_City" title="Dubai International Academic City">Dubai International Academic City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DubaiR_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DubaiR-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> The university works in partnership with the <a href="/wiki/Higher_Colleges_of_Technology" title="Higher Colleges of Technology">Higher Colleges of Technology</a>, the largest post-secondary institution in the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>. Discussions regarding the partnership first emerged in 2004, and was officially launched in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> Through the partnership, the university had offered an undergraduate degree in chemical engineering, civil engineering, financial analysis and risk management, and information technology management.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> The university did not operate, nor manage any facilities in Dubai, with all its facilities belonging to the Higher Colleges of Technology.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> The decision to close the Dubai campus was made by the university's Board of Governors on the 31 October 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-DubaiR_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DubaiR-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus">Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Waterloo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Campus">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>The university's main campus lies within the city of Waterloo, Ontario. The main campus is bordered to the south by Waterloo Park, Wilfred Laurier University to the southeast, residential neighbourhoods to the northeast, east and west, and the <a href="/wiki/Grand_River_Conservation_Authority" title="Grand River Conservation Authority">Laurel Creek Conservation Area</a> to the northwest. Three <a href="/wiki/List_of_numbered_roads_in_Waterloo_Region" title="List of numbered roads in Waterloo Region">numbered roads</a> also intersect the main campus, University Avenue West, Columbia Street West, and Westmount Road North.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> While the main campus is 404 hectares (1,000 acres), the majority of the teaching facilities are centered around a ring road in the southern portion of the main campus.<sup id="cite_ref-size_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-size-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition to its main campus in Waterloo, the university owns several other properties in <a href="/wiki/Cambridge,_Ontario" title="Cambridge, Ontario">Cambridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Huntsville,_Ontario" title="Huntsville, Ontario">Huntsville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kitchener,_Ontario" title="Kitchener, Ontario">Kitchener</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Stratford,_Ontario" title="Stratford, Ontario">Stratford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a>.</p> 
     <p>The buildings at the university vary in age. The oldest building at the university is Graduate House, originally a farmhouse dating back to the 19th century. The oldest building which was erected for the university is Douglas Wright Engineering Building, which was erected in 1958.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> A large majority of the university's buildings, and its ring road, was constructed during the 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> The university's main campus is divided up into three major areas; South Campus, North Campus and the Northwest Campus. The South Campus is the academic core of the university, while the North Campus holds the Research + Technology Park. The Northwest Campus is the least developed area of the main campus, made up primarily of farm fields and an environmental reserve, which divides the Northwest Campus from the North Campus.<sup id="cite_ref-size_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-size-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries_and_museums">Libraries and museums</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Waterloo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Libraries and museums">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Dana_Porter_Arts_Library_in_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="The Dana Porter Library at the University of Waterloo." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Dana_Porter_Arts_Library_in_2009.jpg/175px-Dana_Porter_Arts_Library_in_2009.jpg" width="175" height="245" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Dana_Porter_Arts_Library_in_2009.jpg/263px-Dana_Porter_Arts_Library_in_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Dana_Porter_Arts_Library_in_2009.jpg/350px-Dana_Porter_Arts_Library_in_2009.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Dana_Porter_Arts_Library_in_2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Dana Porter library currently holds the university's main collection for humanities and social science.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Waterloo Libraries include four campus libraries housing more than 1.4 million monograph items and more electronic resources, including e-books, serial titles and databases.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> The university has three libraries located on campus. The Dana Porter Library, which houses the material relating to arts, humanities and social science, the Davis Centre Library, which houses material for engineering, mathematics and science and the Witer Learning Resource Centre, which houses material for the university's School of Optometry and Vision Science. The university's fourth library, the Musagetes Architecture Library, is located in Cambridge, where the university's <a href="/wiki/School_of_Architecture" title="School of Architecture" class="mw-redirect">School of Architecture</a> is located. The libraries of the university's affiliated colleges are also considered a part of the university's library system.<sup id="cite_ref-liblo_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-liblo-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> The university's library system is also a member of the TriUniversity Group (TUG), a partnership between the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Guelph" title="University of Guelph">University of Guelph</a>, University of Waterloo and Wilfred Laurier University. The group provides students and researchers at all three universities with a shared program of library collections and services.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> The group also operates the TUG Annex, a repository for less-used library resources from the three universities.<sup id="cite_ref-liblo_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-liblo-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university also operates the Earth Sciences museum, located on campus in the Centre for Environmental Information Technology.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> The museum is largely used as an earth-science teaching museum for local schools and natural-science interest groups in southern Ontario. The main exhibits at the museum includes the <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">Great Lakes</a>, rocks and minerals, dinosaurs and ice age mammals. The museum's dinosaur exhibit most notably houses a complete cast of an <a href="/wiki/Albertosaurus" title="Albertosaurus">Albertosaurus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> The museum also houses an interactive, simulation mining tunnel which aims to teach sustainable mining practices.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> Another museum which is owned and operated by the university is the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Vision_Science" title="Museum of Vision Science">Museum of Vision Science</a>, which is located at the university's School of Optometry building. The university had also previously operated the <a href="/wiki/Elliott_Avedon_Museum_and_Archive_of_Games" title="Elliott Avedon Museum and Archive of Games">Elliott Avedon Museum and Archive of Games</a>, created by the Department of Recreation and Leisure Studies and previously managed by the university's <a href="/wiki/University_of_Waterloo_Faculty_of_Applied_Health_Sciences" title="University of Waterloo Faculty of Applied Health Sciences">Faculty of Applied Health Sciences</a>. Due to a lack of specific academic interest, in 2009 the decision was made to close the Museum and transfer the collection elsewhere.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Housing_and_student_facilities">Housing and student facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Waterloo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Housing and student facilities">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Mackenzie_King_Village.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Mackenzie_King_Village.jpg/200px-Mackenzie_King_Village.jpg" width="200" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Mackenzie_King_Village.jpg/300px-Mackenzie_King_Village.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Mackenzie_King_Village.jpg/400px-Mackenzie_King_Village.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Mackenzie_King_Village.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Mackenzie King Village residences, constructed in 2002, are the latest set of residences constructed by the university.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The university has seven student residences: the Minota Hagey Residence, UW Place, Ron Eydt Village, Village 1, Mackenzie King Village, Columbia Lake North and South. Students are also allowed to apply into the residences of the university's affiliated colleges. The largest residential village at the university is UW Place, which houses 1,300 first-year students, and 350 upper-year students, while the smallest residence is the Minota Hagey Residence, which houses 70 students and is almost exclusively for upper-year students.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> The newest residence at the university is the Mackenzie King Village, which was constructed in 2002, and houses approximately 320 residents.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> In September 2010, 71.1 percent of first-year students lived on campus, part of the 24.9 percent of the overall undergraduate population which lived on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> Residents are represented by two residential councils at the university, one which represents the students at UW Place, and the other which represents all the other residential villages collectively. Each council organizes their own events, and has their own executive, budget and meetings.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> However, the overall mission of both councils is to act as the official representatives for all residents living at the university's residents.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Student Life Centre is the centre of student governance and student directed social, cultural, entertainment and recreational activities, open seven days a week, year-round. The Student Life Centre contains the offices of a number of student organizations, including the <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Students,_University_of_Waterloo" title="Federation of Students, University of Waterloo">Federation of Students</a>, Residence Council, a number of retail and food services and a variety of club space space and study rooms.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> The idea for a <a href="/wiki/Student_activity_center" title="Student activity center">student centre</a> first emerged during the 1960s, and to raise the necessary funds for the building students began to levy a $10 tuition fee. Construction of the Student Life Centre began in July 1966 and was completed in 1968. Tensions between the university and the student community at the university would soon surface over the management and ownership of the Student Life Centre. The conflict had not been resolved until 1969, when Professor Johnson resigned his position as chairman of the Campus Centre Board, along with his colleague Pim Fitzgerald.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Off_campus_facilities">Off campus facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Waterloo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Off campus facilities">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The university has three satellite campuses, and a number of other facilities located throughout <a href="/wiki/Southern_Ontario" title="Southern Ontario">Southern Ontario</a>. The Centre for Extended Learning is a facility owned and managed by the university and is located in Kitchener, Ontario.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> The Centre for Extended Learning provides pre-university courses, part-time studies, online learning and professional development courses.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> Another facility which is owned and managed by the university is the Waterloo Summit Centre for the Environment, located in Huntsville, Ontario. The facility is a year-round research, teaching and community centre that the university established for ecology, climate change, tourism, land-use planning, and local economic development. Located close to <a href="/wiki/Algonquin_Provincial_Park" title="Algonquin Provincial Park">Algonquin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arrowhead_Provincial_Park" title="Arrowhead Provincial Park">Arrowhead Provincial Park</a>, the centre's facilities are used for research in ecological restoration, and conservation.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:WaterlooArchitectureSchool.jpg" class="image"><img alt="The School of Architecture campus in the background by the Grand River in Cambridge, Ontario." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9d/WaterlooArchitectureSchool.jpg/220px-WaterlooArchitectureSchool.jpg" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9d/WaterlooArchitectureSchool.jpg/330px-WaterlooArchitectureSchool.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9d/WaterlooArchitectureSchool.jpg/440px-WaterlooArchitectureSchool.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:WaterlooArchitectureSchool.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The School of Architecture is located in Cambridge, Ontario, situated next to the Grand River.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The university's School of Architecture currently operates out of a campus in Cambridge, Ontario, on the west bank <a href="/wiki/Grand_River_(Ontario)" title="Grand River (Ontario)">Grand River</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-arch_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arch-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> The architecture campus was the idea of the Cambridge Consortium, a group of Cambridge-business owners, who spearheaded the school's fundraising drive to cover a portion of the $27 million cost of creating the new campus. The school, along with its faculty and students were moved to the new campus in September 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-arch_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arch-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> Since 1979, the School of Architecture also operated an architecture studio in <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> in the neighbourhood of <a href="/wiki/Trastevere" title="Trastevere">Trastevere</a>. The opportunity to work at the studio is offered to fourth-year architecture students.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Another satellite campus of the university is the university's Health Science and Pharmacy Campus, located in Kitchener, Ontario, Ontario. The pharmacy building was designed by <a href="/wiki/Siamak_Hariri" title="Siamak Hariri">Siamak Hariri</a>, and was completed in December 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> While the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Waterloo_School_of_Pharmacy" title="University of Waterloo School of Pharmacy">School of Pharmacy</a> acts as the anchor institution of this campus, both students and faculty of the university's Faculty of Applied Health Sciences also use the facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-campu_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-campu-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> The campus includes a primary care teaching clinic which will integrate clinical care and teaching in pharmacy and optometry. Two other universities also make use of the Health Science and Pharmacy campus. <a href="/wiki/McMaster_University" title="McMaster University">McMaster University</a>'s medical school makes use of the campus as its base for its Waterloo Regional Campus, with 56 of the medical school's students admitted at the regional campus in 2012. Wilfred Laurier University's School of Social Work also uses some of the facilities available on the campus.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university's third satellite campus, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Waterloo_Stratford_Campus" title="University of Waterloo Stratford Campus">Stratford Campus</a>, is located in Stratford, Ontario. The focus for the Stratford campus is on the education in digital arts and media. The idea for the Stratford campus first took shape in October 2006, when the City of Stratford, and the university signed a memorandum regarding the creation of the campus. The first building of the campus was officially opened in September 2010, with construction of the campus's second building beginning in June 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> In November 2009, the university had also signed a memorandum of understanding with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Western_Ontario" title="University of Western Ontario">University of Western Ontario</a> regarding academic initiatives at the Stratford Campus.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> The campus had also notably hosted the first four <a href="/wiki/Canada_3.0" title="Canada 3.0">Canada 3.0</a> forums, before its move to Toronto in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:School_of_Pharmacy_UW_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/School_of_Pharmacy_UW_2013.jpg/220px-School_of_Pharmacy_UW_2013.jpg" width="220" height="196" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/School_of_Pharmacy_UW_2013.jpg/330px-School_of_Pharmacy_UW_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/School_of_Pharmacy_UW_2013.jpg/440px-School_of_Pharmacy_UW_2013.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:School_of_Pharmacy_UW_2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The university's School of Pharmacy is located n the university's Kitchener campus.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sustainability">Sustainability</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Waterloo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Sustainability">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The university currently does not operate an Office of Sustainability. Sustainability initiatives are currently divided between several departmental offices at the university, with the university's plant operations charged with the implementation of sustainability initiatives.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> Prior to 2005, the management of sustainability efforts was conducted by the university's waste management coordinator.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> The university's sustainability initiatives is noted as institution-specific, having not signed any national or international sustainability declaration.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> However, the university, along with the other members from the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Ontario_Universities" title="Council of Ontario Universities">Council of Ontario Universities</a>, signed a pledge in 2009 known as <i>Ontario Universities Committed to a Greener World</i>, with the objective of transforming its campus into a model of environmental responsibility.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In regards to incorporating sustainability into the school experience, the university's School of Environment, Enterprise and Development (SEED) placed first in Canada in the <a href="/wiki/Corporate_Knights" title="Corporate Knights">Corporate Knights</a> 2011 ranking for undergraduate business programs.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> The university campus received a C+ grade from the Sustainable Endowments Institute on its College Sustainability Report Card for 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administration">Administration</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Waterloo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Administration">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>The university operates through a bicameral form of governance, the Board of Governors and the Senate, both enshrined in legislative act, the University of Waterloo Act, 1972.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> The Board has responsibility and control of the university's property and revenues, the conduct of its business and affairs.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> The university's governing act states that the Board shall consist of 36 members, each of whom hold a Canadian citizenship. However, the number of members in the Board for the 2012-2013 academic year is 40.<sup id="cite_ref-bocur_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bocur-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bordoc_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bordoc-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> The Board has eight ex officio members including the university's chancellor, president and the mayors of Kitchener and <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Waterloo,_Ontario" title="List of mayors of Waterloo, Ontario">Waterloo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bocur_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bocur-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> The other 32 members of the Board, are either elected or appointed by the various members of the university community, including alumni, faculty and the student body.<sup id="cite_ref-bordoc_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bordoc-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Senate is responsible for establishing the educational policies of the university and to make recommendations to the Board of Governors with respect to any matter relative to the operation of the university.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> The Senate consists of 24 ex officio positions including the president and chancellor of the university, the vice-presidents, the senior dean of each faculty, the presidents of the undergraduate, graduate and faculty associations, and the presidents and principals of the university's associated colleges. The Senate also consists of 61 other members, appointed or elected by various communities of the university including the faculty of the university, its associated colleges, the student body, and alumni.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The principal acts as the chief executive officer of the university appointed by the Board of Governors, with the approval of the Senate, and is responsible for the administering the affairs of the university, and acts on behalf of the Board with respect to the operational management and control of the university. The president is the chair of the Senate and s member of the Board.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> In March 2011, <a href="/wiki/Feridun_Hamdullahpur" title="Feridun Hamdullahpur">Feridun Hamdullahpur</a> was announced as the sixth president of the university, although he was already the interim president since October 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> The president also holds the position of vice-chancellor, which assumes the duties of chancellor during his absences or during a temporary vacancy in office.<sup id="cite_ref-chanc_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chanc-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> The office of the chancellor is elected by the members of the Senate, in which their term in office is three years, although eligible for renewal. The primary duty of the chancellor is to preside at all Convocations and present candidates for <a href="/wiki/Honorary_degrees" title="Honorary degrees" class="mw-redirect">honorary degrees</a> to the Senate.<sup id="cite_ref-chanc_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chanc-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> The office of the chancellor is currently held by <a href="/wiki/Prem_Watsa" title="Prem Watsa">Prem Watsa</a>, taking over the position in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Affiliated_institutions">Affiliated institutions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Waterloo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Affiliated institutions">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Stpaulsunitedcollege.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f6/Stpaulsunitedcollege.jpg/220px-Stpaulsunitedcollege.jpg" width="220" height="77" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f6/Stpaulsunitedcollege.jpg/330px-Stpaulsunitedcollege.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f6/Stpaulsunitedcollege.jpg/440px-Stpaulsunitedcollege.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Stpaulsunitedcollege.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/St._Paul%27s_University_College" title="St. Paul's University College">St. Paul's University College</a> is one of the four affiliated university colleges currently operated by the university.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The university also operates three affiliated colleges and a federated university. <a href="/wiki/Conrad_Grebel_University_College" title="Conrad Grebel University College">Conrad Grebel University College</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Mennonite" title="Mennonite">Mennonite</a> <a href="/wiki/University_college" title="University college">university college</a> that was chartered in 1961 and is religiously affiliated with the <a href="/wiki/Mennonite_Church_Canada" title="Mennonite Church Canada">Mennonite Church Eastern Canada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-affil_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-affil-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Renison_University_College" title="Renison University College">Renison University College</a> is an <a href="/wiki/Anglican" title="Anglican" class="mw-redirect">Anglican</a> university college chartered in 1959 and entered an affiliation with the University of Waterloo in 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> Renison is religiously affiliated with the <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Church_of_Canada" title="Anglican Church of Canada">Anglican Church of Canada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/St._Jerome%27s_University" title="St. Jerome's University">St. Jerome's University</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic" class="mw-redirect">Roman Catholic</a> university which was founded in 1865. St. Jerome's entered into a federation with the University of Waterloo shortly after the provincial government granted it university status in 1959.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/St._Paul%27s_University_College" title="St. Paul's University College">St. Paul's University College</a> is a university college founded by members of the <a href="/wiki/United_Church_of_Canada" title="United Church of Canada">United Church of Canada</a> in 1962. However, St. Paul's is now operates independently from the United Church and no longer holds any formal or legal relationship.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The three colleges and federated university are all located within the University of Waterloo's main campus, and operate their own residences.<sup id="cite_ref-affil_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-affil-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> Students of these affiliated colleges and federated university, are also academically integrated with the University of Waterloo. Students who study at any of the colleges or university, are also considered registered students of the University of Waterloo. Therefore, in addition to the classes offered at these colleges and federated university, students also have the option to enrol in classes, apply to any of the faculties and graduate as a student from the University of Waterloo.<sup id="cite_ref-affil_72-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-affil-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> Regardless of the affiliated colleges and federated university's religious affiliations, enrolment is not restricted based on the student's religious beliefs.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Finances">Finances</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Waterloo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Finances">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The university completed the 2010?2011 academic year with revenues of $824.684 million and expenses of $763.129 million, yielding a surplus of $61.555 million.<sup id="cite_ref-UWFin_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UWFin-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> Grants and contracts make up the largest source of revenue for the university, followed by academic fees. Salaries make up nearly half of the university's expenses.<sup id="cite_ref-UWFin_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UWFin-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> As of the 30 April 2012, the university's endowment is valued at $261.428 million.<sup id="cite_ref-UWFin_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UWFin-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> The university is registered as an educational charitable organization by <a href="/wiki/Canada_Revenue_Agency" title="Canada Revenue Agency">Canada Revenue Agencysince</a> 1 January 1967. As of 2011, the entire emphasis of the charity is placed on the management and maintenance of the university.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Waterloo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>Waterloo is a publicly funded research university, and a member of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Universities_and_Colleges_of_Canada" title="Association of Universities and Colleges of Canada">Association of Universities and Colleges of Canada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> Waterloo functions on a term-based system, operating year-round on three different terms, fall, winter and spring.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> Undergraduate programs comprise the majority of the school's enrolment, made up of 24,377 full-time and part-time undergraduate students. The university conferred 4,365 bachelor degrees, 237 doctoral degrees, 1,276 master degrees, and 86 first professional degrees in 2010?2011.<sup id="cite_ref-CUDO1_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CUDO1-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Students may apply for financial aid such as the Ontario Student Assistance Program and Canada Student Loans and Grants through the federal and provincial governments. The financial aid provided may come in the form of loans, grants, bursaries, scholarships, fellowships, debt reduction, interest relief, and work programs.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reputation">Reputation</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Waterloo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Reputation">edit</a>]</span></h3>
