           <li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Canadian_university_rankings&amp;action=edit"><span title="Edit this template" style="">e</span></a></li> 
          </ul> 
         </div> </td> 
       </tr> 
      </tbody>
     </table> 
     <p>Waterloo has consistently been ranked as one of the top universities in Canada. According to the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a> (ARWU) rankings, the university ranked 151-200 in the world and seventh in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_ARWU_CAN_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_ARWU_CAN-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> The 2012-2013 <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a> placed Waterloo 226-250 in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_THES_W_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_THES_W-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> The 2012 <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a> ranked the university 191st in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-qsqs_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qsqs-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> In terms of national rankings, <a href="/wiki/Maclean%27s" title="Maclean's">Maclean's</a> ranked Waterloo 3rd in their 2011 comprehensive university rankings.<sup id="cite_ref-Macdoc_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macdoc-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> In an employability survey published by the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Times" title="New York Times" class="mw-redirect">New York Times</a> in October 2011, when CEOs and chairmans were asked to select the top universities which they recruited from, Waterloo placed 106th in the world, and sixth in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Several of Waterloo's programs have also gained recognition nationally and internationally. In the field of statistics and operational research, the university was ranked 32nd in the world, and first in the country by the QS World University Rankings.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> The same rankings had also placed the university 29th in the world, and second in Canada in the field of mathematics.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> Waterloo's engineering program has consistently been ranked within the top 100 universities. The 2012 ARWU's rankings for the field of engineering, technology and computer sciences, had ranked the university 43rd in the world and second in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_ARWU_ENG_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_ARWU_ENG-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> In the 2012 rankings of the top engineering schools in the world by <a href="/wiki/Business_Insider" title="Business Insider">Business Insider</a>, the university ranked 29th in the world, and first in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> In the specific field of computer science and information systems, the 2013 QS World University Rankings had placed the university 27th in the world, and second in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Waterloo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Waterloo_Nano_Building.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/University_of_Waterloo_Nano_Building.jpg/200px-University_of_Waterloo_Nano_Building.jpg" width="200" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/University_of_Waterloo_Nano_Building.jpg/300px-University_of_Waterloo_Nano_Building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/University_of_Waterloo_Nano_Building.jpg/400px-University_of_Waterloo_Nano_Building.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Waterloo_Nano_Building.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The university's institutes for both 
        <a href="/wiki/Waterloo_Institute_for_Nanotechnology" title="Waterloo Institute for Nanotechnology">nanotechnology</a> and 
        <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Quantum_Computing" title="Institute for Quantum Computing">quantum computing</a> are located in the Mike and Ophelia Lazaridis Quantum-Nano Centre.
        <sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The university currently operates and manages 41 research centres and institutes, including the <a href="/wiki/Centre_for_Applied_Cryptographic_Research" title="Centre for Applied Cryptographic Research">Centre for Applied Cryptographic Research</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Waterloo_Institute_for_Nanotechnology" title="Waterloo Institute for Nanotechnology">Waterloo Institute for Nanotechnology</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Centre_for_Education_in_Mathematics_and_Computing" title="Centre for Education in Mathematics and Computing">Centre for Education in Mathematics and Computing</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Quantum_Computing" title="Institute for Quantum Computing">Institute for Quantum Computing</a>. Official recognition and designation of all centres and institutes requires the approval of the university's Senate.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> In Research Infosource's 2011 ranking of Canada's 50 top research universities, Waterloo was ranked 15th, with a sponsored research income of $144.299 million, averaging $143,300 per faculty member.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Higher_Education_Evaluation_and_Accreditation_Council_of_Taiwan" title="Higher Education Evaluation and Accreditation Council of Taiwan">Higher Education Evaluation and Accreditation Council of Taiwan</a> (HEEACT), an organization which evaluates universities based on their scientific paper's performances, ranked Waterloo 283rd in the world and 13th nationally in its 2011 rankings.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> In the 2011 University Ranking by Academic Performance (URAP), which rates universities based off their research performance, Waterloo was ranked 185th in the world and tenth in Canada. Waterloo's research in the field of engineering has also received a number of accolades. In the 2011 URAP rankings, Waterloo's research performance in the field of engineering was ranked 43rd in the world, and second in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> In the 2011 HEEACT rankings, Waterloo's research performance in the field of engineering was ranked 74th in the world, and second in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Admission">Admission</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Waterloo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Admission">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The requirements for admission differ between students from Ontario, other provinces in Canada, and international students due to the lack of uniformity in marking schemes. For students applying from an Ontario secondary school, university's admissions office maintains that an average of at least 79 percent is required for minimum consideration, although a higher averages are required for admission to programs in which the demand for places by qualified applicants exceeds the number of places available. The actual minimum averages required for these programs are determined each year on the basis of the number and qualification of applicants and the number of available spaces.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> The secondary school averages for full-time, first year students for the 2011-2012 academic year was 87.7 percent. The program with the highest admission average during that year was mathematics, with an admission average of 90.6 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> The retention rate of the university's first-time, full-time first year students in 2009 was 89.4 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Students may apply for financial aid such as the <a href="/wiki/Ontario_Student_Assistance_Program" title="Ontario Student Assistance Program">Ontario Student Assistance Program</a> and <a href="/wiki/Student_loans_in_Canada" title="Student loans in Canada">Canada Student Loans and Grants</a> through the federal and provincial governments. The financial aid provided may come in the form of loans, grants, bursaries, scholarships, fellowships, debt reduction, interest relief, and work programs.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Waterloo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Pi_day_uw_2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Pi_day_uw_2007.jpg/175px-Pi_day_uw_2007.jpg" width="175" height="233" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Pi_day_uw_2007.jpg/263px-Pi_day_uw_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Pi_day_uw_2007.jpg/350px-Pi_day_uw_2007.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Pi_day_uw_2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Pi_Day" title="Pi Day">Pi Day</a>, which commemorates the 
        <a href="/wiki/Mathematical_constant" title="Mathematical constant">mathematical constant</a>, is celebrated annually by the university's student body.
        <sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The two main student unions on administrative and policy issues is the <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Students,_University_of_Waterloo" title="Federation of Students, University of Waterloo">Federation of Students</a> for all undergraduate students and the Graduate Student Association for graduate students.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> The Federation of Students was created in 1967. The Federation of Students operates seven businesses, eight student services and encompasses nearly 200 clubs. The federation also oversees the university's Orientation Week, Welcome Week and all other special events and concerts held on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> The organizations and clubs accredited by the Federation of Students cover a wide range of interests including academics, culture, religion, social issues, and recreation.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> Many of them are centred on the university's <a href="/wiki/Student_activity_centre" title="Student activity centre" class="mw-redirect">student activity centre</a>, the Student Life Centre. As of June 2007, neither the university administration, nor the student union recognize <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities_in_North_America" title="Fraternities and sororities in North America">fraternities and sororities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> There are currently two active fraternities which operate as non-accredited off-campus organizations, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Epsilon_Pi" title="Alpha Epsilon Pi">Alpha Epsilon Pi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Chi" title="Sigma Chi">Sigma Chi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> Two sororities also operate as non-accredited off-campus organizations, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Omicron_Pi" title="Alpha Omicron Pi">Alpha Omicron Pi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Kappa_Gamma" title="Kappa Kappa Gamma">Kappa Kappa Gamma</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The official <a href="/wiki/Student_newspaper" title="Student newspaper">student newspaper</a> at the university is the <a href="/wiki/Imprint_(newspaper)" title="Imprint (newspaper)">Imprint</a>, which publishes a weekly edition during the fall and winter semesters and a biweekly edition for the spring and summer semesters.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Chevron" title="The Chevron">The Chevron</a>, previously called the The Coryphaeus until 1966, was previously the official student newspaper of the student union.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> However, by the late 1960s and 1970s, the newspaper's increasingly left-wing agenda had resulted in the Federation of Students to freeze funding for The Chevron in 1976, with its status as the official student newspaper removed by referendum in November 1978.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-iwarr_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iwarr-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> The university's Journalism Club, made up of former staff from The Chevron, along with other student, created another newspaper known as the Imprint in 1978. In March 1979, a referendum officially made the Imprint the official newspaper of the student union.<sup id="cite_ref-iwarr_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iwarr-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> The university also operates a <a href="/wiki/Campus_radio" title="Campus radio">campus radio</a> station, <a href="/wiki/CKMS-FM" title="CKMS-FM">CKMS-FM</a>, colloquially known as SoundFM. The radio station was officially incorporated in 1977.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Waterloo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Waterloo_Warriors" title="Waterloo Warriors">Waterloo Warriors</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Sport teams at the University of Waterloo are known as the <a href="/wiki/Waterloo_Warriors" title="Waterloo Warriors">Waterloo Warriors</a>. The Warriors sports teams participate in the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Interuniversity_Sport" title="Canadian Interuniversity Sport">Canadian Interuniversity Sport</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Ontario_University_Athletics" title="Ontario University Athletics">Ontario University Athletics</a> conference for most varsity sports. Varsity teams at the university currently include badminton, baseball, basketball, cross country, curling, field hockey, figure skating, Canadian football, golf, hockey, Nordic skiing, rugby, soccer, squash, swimming, track and field, tennis and volleyball. The athletics program at the university dates back to 1957, when students of Waterloo College Associate Faculties participated in the sports program of Waterloo College (present-day Wilfred Laurier University). The university would have its own independent team with the Associate Faculties officially became the University of Waterloo.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> Both the university's varsity teams, as well as the university's recreational sports programs are operated and managed by the Department of Athletics and Recreational Activity.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university has a number of athletic facilities open to both their varsity teams as well as to their students. The stadium with the largest seating capacity at the university is <a href="/wiki/Warrior_Field" title="Warrior Field">Warrior Field</a>. The field currently is home to the varsity field hockey and football teams, and hosts the university's recreational flag football and soccer activities. The has a seating capacity of 5,400.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> Other facilities at the university includes the Physical Activity Complex, which houses two gymnasiums, beach volleyball courts, squash rooms, and a swimming pool, and is also home to the university's varsity badminton, basketball, squash, swimming and volleyball teams.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> The Columbia Ice Field was constructed in 1983 and currently houses the university's hockey team home rink, with a seating capacity of 700. The Ice Field had since been expanded twice in 1990 and 2003 and now includes three gyms, and a number of fitness centres.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> Including the university's football field, the university also manages seven outdoor playing fields, with Fields 1 and 2 reserved for the varsity soccer and rugby teams. The rest of the fields are used by the university's recreational sports programs.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Insignias_and_other_representations">Insignias and other representations</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Waterloo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Insignias and other representations">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Coat_of_Arms">Coat of Arms</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Waterloo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Coat of Arms">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The coat of arms was first adopted by the university in October 1961, but was only officially granted by the <a href="/wiki/Lord_Lyon_King_of_Arms" title="Lord Lyon King of Arms">Lord Lyon King of Arms</a> in August 1987.<sup id="cite_ref-comot_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-comot-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> The coat of arms would not be registered with the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Heraldic_Authority" title="Canadian Heraldic Authority">Canadian Heraldic Authority</a> until 15 February 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> Four variations of the coat of arms existed in the university's history. The first was used from 1961 to 1996, when the second bright-yellow shield using slightly different shaped lions was introduced. The yellow background was dulled in 2000, and finally, the original lions were reintroduced in 2010 in conjunction with the attempt to replace the use of the coat of arms with a futuristic <i>W</i> logo.<sup id="cite_ref-coa_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coa-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> The proposed logo was eventually rejected, after student opposition.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The red-on-gold lions on the university's arms were adopted from the <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Wellesley,_1st_Duke_of_Wellington" title="Arthur Wellesley, 1st Duke of Wellington">Arthur Wellesley, 1st Duke of Wellington</a>, who defeated <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Waterloo" title="Battle of Waterloo">Battle of Waterloo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-coa_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coa-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> The City of Waterloo was named after an area just south of <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, where the battle occurred.<sup id="cite_ref-name_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-name-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> The chevron on the arms was adopted from the arms of <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Kitchener,_1st_Earl_Kitchener" title="Herbert Kitchener, 1st Earl Kitchener">Herbert Kitchener, 1st Earl Kitchener</a>, Field Marshal with the British Army during World War I. The black and white pattern used on the chevron was adopted from the colours of <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussia</a>, as homage to the German heritage of the area.<sup id="cite_ref-coa_130-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coa-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> The City of Kitchener was originally known as Berlin, but was renamed after the Kitchener in 1916, at the height of the war.<sup id="cite_ref-name_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-name-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Motto_and_songs">Motto and songs</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Waterloo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Motto and songs">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The university's motto, is <i>Concordia cum veritate</i>. The Latin motto is literally translated as &quot;In Harmony with Truth&quot;. The motto was introduced along with the university coat of arms back in October 1961.<sup id="cite_ref-comot_128-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-comot-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> A number of songs are commonly played and sung at various events such as <a href="/wiki/Graduation" title="Graduation">commencement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Convocation" title="Convocation">convocation</a>, and athletic contests. The main song of the university is known as the Black and White and Gold. The words of the song were created by K. D. Fryer and H. F. Davis, while the composition of the music was created by <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Kunz_(composer)" title="Alfred Kunz (composer)">Alfred Kunz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_alumni_and_faculty">Notable alumni and faculty</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Waterloo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Notable alumni and faculty">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Mike_Lazaridis.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Mike Lazaridis co-founder of Research in Motion, and former chancellor of the university." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Mike_Lazaridis.jpg/200px-Mike_Lazaridis.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Mike_Lazaridis.jpg/300px-Mike_Lazaridis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Mike_Lazaridis.jpg/400px-Mike_Lazaridis.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Mike_Lazaridis.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Mike_Lazaridis" title="Mike Lazaridis">Mike Lazaridis</a> was a student at Waterloo, its former chancellor, and the co-founder and former co-CEO of Research in Motion
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Waterloo_people" title="List of University of Waterloo people">List of University of Waterloo people</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Waterloo's graduates have found success in a variety of fields, serving at the heads of diverse institutions both in the public and private sector. Over 160,900 people have graduated from Waterloo residing in over 144 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-About_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> Waterloo graduates have accumulated a number of awards including the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Governor_General%27s_Award" title="Governor General's Award" class="mw-redirect">Governor General's Award</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_Scholarships" title="Rhodes Scholarships" class="mw-redirect">Rhodes Scholarships</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Mundell" title="Robert Mundell">Robert Mundell</a>, the recipient of the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Memorial_Prize_in_Economic_Sciences" title="Nobel Memorial Prize in Economic Sciences">Nobel Memorial Prize in Economic Sciences</a>, also served as the chairman of the university's economic's department.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>A significant number of prominent business leaders have worked or studied at Waterloo. Examples include <a href="/wiki/John_Baker_(entrepreneur)" title="John Baker (entrepreneur)">John Baker</a>, founder of <a href="/wiki/Desire2Learn" title="Desire2Learn">Desire2Learn</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/David_Cheriton" title="David Cheriton">David Cheriton</a>, co-founder and chief scientist of <a href="/wiki/Arista_Networks" title="Arista Networks">Arista Networks</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mike_Lazaridis" title="Mike Lazaridis">Mike Lazaridis</a>, co-founder and former co-CEO of <a href="/wiki/Research_in_Motion" title="Research in Motion" class="mw-redirect">Research in Motion</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Prem_Watsa" title="Prem Watsa">Prem Watsa</a>, chairman of <a href="/wiki/Fairfax_Financial" title="Fairfax Financial">Fairfax Financial</a> and the current chancellor of the Waterloo,<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Steven_Woods" title="Steven Woods">Steven Woods</a>, co-founder of <a href="/wiki/NeoEdge_Networks" title="NeoEdge Networks">NeoEdge Networks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quack.com" title="Quack.com">Quack.com</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup> and co-founders of <a href="/wiki/Waterloo_Maple" title="Waterloo Maple">Waterloo Maple</a>, <a href="/wiki/Keith_Geddes" title="Keith Geddes">Keith Geddes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gaston_Gonnet" title="Gaston Gonnet">Gaston Gonnet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup> Gonnet was also the co-founder of <a href="/wiki/Open_Text_Corporation" title="Open Text Corporation">Open Text Corporation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> Several university's faculty members and students have also gained local and national prominence for serving in government. <a href="/wiki/David_Johnston" title="David Johnston">David Johnston</a>, the former president of Waterloo, currently serves as the <a href="/wiki/Governor_General_of_Canada" title="Governor General of Canada">Governor General of Canada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>A number of the university's faculty and students have also gained prominence in the field of computing sciences. Examples include <a href="/wiki/QNX" title="QNX">QNX</a> operating systems co-creators <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Bell_(QNX)" title="Gordon Bell (QNX)">Gordon Bell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dan_Dodge" title="Dan Dodge">Dan Dodge</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rasmus_Lerdorf" title="Rasmus Lerdorf">Rasmus Lerdorf</a>, the creator of the <a href="/wiki/PHP" title="PHP">PHP</a> scripting language,<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Peter_Buhr" title="Peter Buhr">Peter Buhr</a>, the creator of the <a href="/wiki/%CE%9CC%2B%2B" title="?C++">?C++</a> programming language,<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Cormack" title="Gordon Cormack">Gordon Cormack</a>, the co-creator of <a href="/wiki/Dynamic_Markov_compression" title="Dynamic Markov compression">Dynamic Markov compression</a> algorithm,<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Ric_Holt" title="Ric Holt">Ric Holt</a>, co-creator of several programming languages, most notably <a href="/wiki/Turing_(programming_language)" title="Turing (programming language)">Turing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Waterloo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a>]</span></h2>
